## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This is a population growth rate modeling task where dP/dt is expressed as a function of population P and time t. Classical population dynamics models describe how growth rate depends on current population size through density-dependent feedback mechanisms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited growth, Malthusian model)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (asymmetric sigmoidal growth)
- Theta-logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with shape parameter)
- Allee effect (strong): dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P) (growth with minimum viable population)
- Allee effect (weak): dP_dt = c0 * P * (P + c1) * (1 - c2 * P) (reduced growth at low density without extinction threshold)
- Von Bertalanffy-type: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolism vs catabolism scaling)
- Beverton-Holt continuous: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) - c2 * P (growth with density-dependent resource limitation)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (generalized density-dependent growth)
- Time-varying Malthusian: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t) (exponential growth with time-varying rate)
- Logistic with time-varying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P * exp(c2 * t)) (logistic with changing carrying capacity)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) * (c1 * P)**c3 (flexible asymmetric growth)
- Quadratic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (polynomial density effects)
- Harvesting model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (logistic growth with constant harvesting)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dP/dt is proportional to P at low densities, the model has a linear per-capita growth rate at small P → multiplicative P factor in the formula
- If dP/dt becomes negative at large P, a negative quadratic term P² indicates carrying capacity limitation → look for c0*P - c1*P² structure
- If dP/dt is negative at both very small and very large P, an Allee effect is present → cubic polynomial in P with alternating signs
- If the per-capita growth rate dP_dt/P depends on time, the environment is non-stationary → include explicit t-dependent terms multiplied by P
- If dP/dt has a single maximum at intermediate P, this is characteristic of logistic-type growth → quadratic or rational function of P
- If dP/dt/P vs P shows a concave (not linear) relationship, theta-logistic or Gompertz is more appropriate than standard logistic → use log(P) or P**c terms
- If growth rate saturates rather than linearly decreasing with P, rational forms P/(1+cP) are preferred over polynomial forms
- If the system has a non-zero stable equilibrium, the growth rate function must cross zero with negative slope at that point → root-finding structure in f(P)

## Analysis

The GT expression is:
$$f(P) = 0.954 \cdot (1 - P/96.907) \cdot P + 0.954 \cdot P^{0.333}$$

Expanding:
$$f(P) = 0.954 \cdot P - \frac{0.954}{96.907} \cdot P^2 + 0.954 \cdot P^{1/3}$$
$$f(P) = -0.009845 \cdot P^2 + 0.954 \cdot P + 0.954 \cdot P^{1/3}$$

This is of the form: $a \cdot P^2 + b \cdot P + c \cdot P^{1/3}$, with no dependence on $t$.

**Candidate 1**: `P**2*c0 + P*c1 + P/(P*c2 + c3) + P**c4*c5 + c6 + 1/(P*c2 + c3)`

Set c2 = 0, then P/(P*c2 + c3) = P/c3 and 1/(P*c2 + c3) = 1/c3. This gives:
$$c0 \cdot P^2 + (c1 + 1/c3) \cdot P + c5 \cdot P^{c4} + c6 + 1/c3$$

Set c4 = 1/3, c5 = 0.954, c0 = -0.009845, and choose c3 such that c1 + 1/c3 = 0.954, and c6 + 1/c3 = 0. This works: pick c3 = large (or any value) and adjust c1 and c6. For instance, let c3 = 1000, then 1/c3 ≈ 0.001, c1 ≈ 0.953, c6 ≈ -0.001. This matches. ✓

**Candidate 9**: `P**2*c0 + P*c1 + P/(P*c2 + c3) + P**c4*c5 + 1/(P + c3)`

Set c2 = 0, then P/(P*c2 + c3) = P/c3 and 1/(P + c3) remains as 1/(P + c3), which introduces a term dependent on P that can't be absorbed. We'd need 1/(P + c3) = 0, but that's impossible for all P. However, if we try c2 = 0 and c3 → ∞, both P/c3 → 0 and 1/(P+c3) → 0, but then we lose the linear P term... Let me reconsider.

Actually, we can keep c2 ≠ 0. We need: P/(P*c2 + c3) + 1/(P + c3) to combine with the other terms. This gets complicated and the rational terms in P can't easily produce a pure polynomial + power form.

**Candidate 1 is the cleanest match.** With c2 = 0:
- c0 = -0.009845 (coefficient of P²)
- c4 = 1/3, c5 = 0.954 (gives 0.954·P^{1/3})
- c3 = any nonzero value, say c3 = K
- c1 = 0.954 - 1/K (so c1 + 1/K = 0.954, the coefficient of P)
- c6 = -1/K (so c6 + 1/c3 = 0, eliminating the constant)

This exactly reproduces $-0.009845 P^2 + 0.954 P + 0.954 P^{1/3}$.

**Matching candidate: Formula 1**

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the Ground Truth:

**GT: 0.954*(1 - P/96.907)*P + 0.954*P^(1/3)**

Expanding: **GT = 0.954*P - (0.954/96.907)*P² + 0.954*P^(1/3)**

So GT = c_a*P² + c_b*P + c_c*P^(1/3) where:
- c_a = -0.954/96.907 ≈ -0.00984
- c_b = 0.954
- c_c = 0.954

Let me check each candidate for the ability to match these three terms exactly.

### Candidate 1:
`P²*c0 + P*c1 + P/(P*c2 + c3) + P^c4*c5 + c6 + 1/(P*c2 + c3)`

### Candidate 2:

Combining over common denominator (P+c1):
= [c0*P³ + (c2+1)*P² + (c1+c3+c4)*P + (c5+c6+c7)] / (P+c1)

Performing polynomial division of numerator by (P+c1):

This is a rational function that simplifies to a polynomial plus a term like K/(P+c1). The GT requires P^(1/3), which cannot be produced by rational functions.
